 5. The establishment of the texts and textual criticism I have decided to edit the H, E, and 0 texts as being the most important ones (sections 3.1-3.6). It was desirable to replace the H text by the SI text, but this proved impossible (section 5.1 below). 5. i . The SI and II texts It is desirable to reconstruct and edit the SI text since it is the oldest stage of St. Birgitta's own version that can be distinguished from among the MSS, but this is not possible, mainly because E is a revised version. The lost H MS and the lost E MS can both be reconstructed from the extant II and MSS, and whenever II and E agree, they offer the readings of SZ. The difficulties arise when H and E disagree. First of all, it is impossible even to specify the actual content of SI: paragraphs 1-34, 42-44 and 271-317 (which were in H but not in E) either were present in SI and were omitted when E was produced or were lacking in SZ and were added somewhere between S2, and n in the stemma (which is quite plausible, since they or, at least, some of them are later addi- tions to the core of the RS; see section 3.1). The uncertainty is equally em- barrassing when we come to single passages in which H and E disagree. There are certain guiding principles for determining the SI reading in such passages,126 but on most occasions they fail and the reading of SI remains doubtful. Under these circumstances, any attempt to restore the SI text completely would result only in an unreliable mixture based on a considerable amount of arbitrary selection and it was judged more satisfactory to abstain from such attempts and to edit the H text instead. Since both the H and E texts have been edited, the reader is enabled to form his own opinion on the reading of SI in those Since E is a revised version, it is a priori more likely that Si had the H readings than the E readings. This is confirmed in some passages by an analysis of the contents of the H and E texts. In the H text, Christ on several occasions appears speaking in the first person (for example, 141 corpus meum; 237 potuissem), whereas E offers the third person (corpus christi and potuisset deus respectively), a difference which led to the designations regula in prima persona and regula in tercia persona (cf. section 3 and subsection 4.4.2 (a)). This is certainly a change in E in order to remove the status of direct revelation and SI accordingly had the II readings. An analogous reasoning holds true of the passages in which changes in E classify the RS as subordinate to the Regula Augustini and fl certainly had the H readings in these (for example, i 12 regulam istam tenere in the II text and secundum regulam sancti augustini et constituciones istas beate birgitte viuere in the E text; other examples in subsection 4.4.2 (b) and (d)). On the other hand, there are passages in which SZ apparently had the readings, not the H readings, to judge from a comparison with the OSAa text (see below). To sum up, when H and E agree, their reading was in 1-2; when they disagree, the reading of f/ is doubtful, but it is a priori more likely that fl had the II reading than the E reading. A more reliable decision on the reading of fl is obtainable only in a few such passages from a study of the general policy of the E revisers and from a comparison with OSA (outlined below). 126 
 
 
 
 
 5.1. THE 52 AND II TEXTS 73 passages which may interest him, by comparing these two texts (considering also OSAa, which is available in Klemming's edition [section 2.3] whenever the II and E texts diller; cf. below). The establishment of the II text requires some methodological considerations. A standard procedure for editorial work implies a reconstruction of an archetype from the MSS ("recension, an examination whether the readings of the arche- type were in the author's autograph or not ("examinatio") and an emending of those which turn out not to have been in the autograph ("divinatio", "emen- dation. This process does not apply to the H text. The lost II MS is just an ordinary MS within the tradition and the autograph is either SZ or (as is more probable) some lost MS above 52.127 Accordingly, the lost H MS certainly contained errors (just like other MSS) and these errors should be incorporated in the printed II text; it would be methodologically inconsistent to correct such errors (thus introducing some SI readings into the II text here and there), the aim having once been necessarily defined as a reconstruction of the 11 MS, not of n (or some autograph). In the following passages, the readings of the II MS seem to be such errors (mostly omissions), committed probably by the II scribe, and SI is likely to have had the E readings, not the II readings; this assumption is based on the fact that the E readings are supported by the OSAa MS, which is located above both H and L:128 170 confessor (section 4.1); 178 qui omni etc. (section 4.1); 188 cum ad (section 4.1); 195 augetur po P' K P Cea Gh generatur If Sea Kf Be0 V födhis OSAa; 212 inhabitancium 1313 P1 K P Cea Gh inhabitancium monasterium If Sea Kf Bep V thera ... som byggia j clostreno OSAa; 217 habita deliberacione po P1 K P Cea Gh habita deliberacione super hoc If se. Kf Be0 V aff wäl forhugxadom fortanka ther owir OSAa; 228 in possessione propria po P1 K P Cea Gh in possessione propria monasterii If Sea Kf BO V j clostersins ägho OSAa; 231 profiteatur po Pr K Cea Gh proficiatur P profiteatur in ista religione If Sea Kf BO V göri professionem j tässo renliffue OSAa; 235 sic sorores etc. (section 4.1); 267 legant po Pf K P Cea Gh cogitent If Sea Kf BO cogitant V tänkin OSAa (cf. note 38 and subsection 4.2.4). These are the most manifest examples and there are some more which are, however, less obvious.129 In § 75 vere/veris the adjective veris of the II text is probably a H error since the syntax demands the adverb (i.e. the autograph probably had vere which has been preserved in E). It may even be meaningless to talk of an autograph, since the text was apparently created gradually (section 3.1). 128 The readings of the H MS are beyond doubt in these passages, owing to the consensus be- tween the H MSS on which the H text is based, viz. pf) Pf K P Cea Gh, and the same statement holds true of the readings of the E MS.  74 5. TEXTUAL CRITICISM The status of the H text, as outlined above, implies that syntactical, con- textual and rhythmical considerations have a very limited value in establishing the II text in passages in which the II MSS differ. No reading can be rejected because it is inferior or even apparently erroneous from the point of view of syntax or content, since the II MS contained errors and the main stress must be laid on the actual comparison of the MSS. The H MSS po P' K P Cea Gh have been chosen as the basis for the reconstruction of the H text for the following reasons and have been used according to the following principles. The g group is represented by po alone, since the texts of L and Ae are con- taminated. The n MS is reconstructed from K and P and since one of these MSS, probably K, offers a contaminated text, it has been taken as a criterion that K P give the text of n when they agree; when they disagree, either of the two readings may have been in n . The (p MS is reconstructed from a comparison between g Pf when they agree, they offer the reading of cp but when they disagree, any of their readings may have been in (p. The reading of II, finally, is determined from a comparison between cp Cea Gh. These principles have been followed throughout in §§ 5-317 of the II text. The p7 MS has been used along- side po Pf K P Cea Gh whenever p7 has the text (i.e. in §§ 2-3, 5-11, 13, 15-23, 25-34, 271, 273-278, 280-288, 290-304 and 306-317), thus rendering the reconstruction of t more reliable. Paragraphs 1-4 are not in all of the po Pf K P Cea Gh MSS; § i is in po PI K P (Cea Gh have another version [subsections 4.2.1 and 5.1.1 (e)]) and has been edited from these MSS and from L; §§ 2-3 are also in po Pf K P (but not in Cea Gh) and have been edited from these MSS and from L Ae p7; § 4, finally, is in K P Cea Gh (not in po Pf) and has been edited from these MSS and from Ae. In establishing the H text, it is, however, not sufficient to consider the II MSS only. The lost E MS (= the reconstructed E text) must also always be regarded, since it is closely related with H via SI Such comparisons are possible in §§ 48-267 (but not in §§ 1-44 and 271-317, which were not in E), except for the headings and some single passages in which E was so reworked that comparisons are meaningless. When E fails, one may sometimes compare the OSAa text in a similar way, since it is located above H (the OSAa text is some- times given in the apparatus of the H text). In subsections 5.1.1-5.1.2 below, I deal with passages in which the re- constrution of the H text encounters more or less severe difficulties. The passages are distributed in two groups, according to the possibilities of com- paring E and OSAa. 5.1.1. Comparisons possible with E or OSAa. The H reading is determined from a comparison between cp (reconstructed as outlined above), Cea and Gh, with due con- sideration of E and, when E fails, of OSAa. (a) In some passages cp may have had either of two or more readings, one of which is also in Cea Gh. The reading offered by some of the (f) MSS, and Cea Gh was almost certainly in H whenever it is supported by E (as is the case in nearly all such passages,

THE S2 AND II TEXTS 75 for example, 159 vanitate P' K Cea Gh P Sea Kf Beo V natiuitate 03 P [cf. note 51]) or by OSAa (when E does not have the text or is reworked, for example, 167 cum consilio episcopi eligatur K [consilio episcopi in ras. There are, however, a few cases in which Cea Gh support one of the presumptive (1:0 readings and E another: 72 festis 03 K2 P Cea Gh festiuis Kl (?) pf p Sea Kf Ber3 V; 88 incipient P' (in incipiant corr. P1) K Cea Gh incipiant pf3 P If Sea Kf BO V; 104 descendet p0 P' P le BO V descendat K Cea Gh P Sea (cf. subsection 5.2.1); 164 curia 03 K P K" BO V curiam In Cea Gh P Sea (cf. subsection 5.2.1). These passages are more or less dubious. In § 72, some parallels are in favour offestis,13° and this reading has been printed. In §§ 104 and 164, the distribution among the MSS is to some extent in favour of descendet and curia (since these readings are supported by the majority of the q MSS [they were also in E; see subsection 5.2.1 ]), whereas the decision is even harder in § 88;1 descendet, curia and incipient have been printed.131 The words festus/festiuus occur in six other passages (§§ 65, 67, 84, 174, 181 and 228) and in these festiuus has sometimes been substituted for festus in different MSS (67 festiuis K' [?] P V [and Ne Oe of the al text]; 84 festiuis P), whereas festiuus is never replaced by festus; this points to H having had festis in § 72, festiuis being errors in K" and Pf. The objection may be raised that taking festis in H in § 72 seems to imply that this word was changed to festiuis in E, which would be against the practice of the E revisers, who normally retained the H readings (festus retained in §§ 67, 174; festiuus retained in §§ 181, 228; festis changed to festiuitatibus in § 84). But this objection is only illusory, since the H MS used by the E revisers is not known to us and could perfectly weil have had festiuis (as an error), in which case the E revisers did not change anything at all but just accepted the reading of their original (cf. note 137). 131 The passages 88 incipient and 104 descendet raise the problem of choosing between the future indicative and the present subjunctive in instructions and exhortations in the third person singular/plural. Since this problem recurs in the subsequent discussions, I insert here an in- vestigation based on a sample of the text, viz. §§ 48-164. In these paragraphs of the H text, there are 45 instances with the future indicative (for example, 67 cantabunt, 85 licebit, 88 ieiunabunt, 94 abstinebunt, 150 erunt, 162 recipiet) and 67 with the present subjunctive (for example, 52 habeant, 64 sit, 81 ingrediatur, 105 subiungat, 122 muniat, 139 vocet). Phonetic distinctness seems to have been one of the factors determining the choice. Of the 45 instances with the future indicative, no less than 35 contain verbs, the future forms of which are distinctly separate from the present indicative/subjunctive forms (verbs of the first and second conjuga- tions and esse, as in the examples from §§ 67, 85, 88, 94 and i5o), whereas in the remaining E) instances there are verbs lacking such a sharp distinction (verbs of the third and fourth con- jugations as in § 162). Of the 67 instances with the present subjunctive, there are only 16 pas- sages with "distinct" verbs (§§ 52, 64 and 139); the other 51 contain "indistinct" verbs (§§ 81, 105 and 122). There are even transitions in coordinations, for example, io8 statuatur ... con- secrabit. In single MSS within the H group, the present subjunctive is sometimes substituted for the future indicative and vice versa; neither type of change is obviously more frequent than the other. So much for the H text. The mood of the H text is generally retained in E (as in the examples given above). Out of the total of 1 1 2 examined cases, E has another mood in 6 only and then always the present subjunctive, instead of the future indicative, for example, 72 cantabitur ... cantabunt in the H text and cantetur ... cantabunt in the E text; 117 incipiet in the H text and incipiat in the E text; 135 conuertet ... imponat in the H text and conuertat ... imponat in the E text. I have checked throughout the entire text that this rule holds true, viz. that E sometimes offers the present subjunctive instead of the future indicative of the H text 130

The E text The lost E MS is the bull sealed and issued by the papal chancellery and after- wards brought to Vadstena. The reconstruction is concentrated only on this document, which had legal validity, not on some draft in the chancellery which must have been behind it. MSS, the Kf MS, the Ber MS and the V MS respectively (the connection of Dea is dubious and it is open to doubt whether it forms a branch of its own or not).  5.2. THE E TEXT 79 the II group) and the E text has been established from a comparison between them, with due consideration of the lost H MS (= the reconstructed II text), which is closely related to E via the SZ source used by the E revisers.137 The existence of more than two stemma branches renders the reconstructed E text comparatively reliable in most passages. The E MS, being the bull delivered from the papal chancellery, is merely a copy of some draft in the chancellery and was probably very carefully checked against this draft, since it was to have legal validity. Yet there is still the possibi- lity that some minor errors remained undiscovered in the E MS, and I have assumed that this happened in 46b perlectis If se. Kf V ex prelatis in perlectis (?) corr. Be0. The E MS apparently had perlectis but, as far as I can see, this makes no sense and may be an error which arose in E; I would suggest that the reading intended, i.e. the reading of the draft behind E, may have been. perleccio.138 Nevertheless, perlectis has been printed, since the aim is to re- construct the legal document E, not the draft. There may be another E error in 6o non deforis corrugatum If Sea Kf Bef3 V, which was apparently the reading of E; the lost H MS had non sit deforis corrugatum. The nominal sentence of E is a very hard construction and it seems out of the question that the E revisers deliberately removed a sit from their S2 source; it is more plausible that the draft had sit and that it dropped out when E was produced and this was not noticed in the subsequent checking.139 The reading seruaturum in § 46j gives the impression of being an error in E for seruaturis or seruandum in the draft but since the future participle may sometimes be used in an intransitive/passive sense, the draft may have had seruaturum (cf. D. Norberg, Syntaktische Forsch- ungen auf dem Gebiete des Spätlateins und des fruhen Mittellateins, Uppsala universitets årsskrift 1943, 9, Uppsala 1943, pp• 193 if., with examples [especially Lex Visigoth. 3.1.5 on p. 196] and further references). The reading et confessa fuerit in E 189 may also be a E error. The status of the E text outlined above implies that syntactical and con- textual considerations may be used to a certain extent in establishing the text. One may at least assume that the E revisers never accepted such readings It is important to emphasize that the lost n MS (= the reconstructed n text) was not the MS used by the E revisers when they produced the E text. The source was a lost n MS (hence- forth called the SI source) and this MS may have differed—and probably did differ—in many passages from the reconstructed II text. Such differences may explain why the E text some- times differs from the II text in trifling details; the differences may have already been present in the E revisers' SZ source and the revisers are not responsible for them, since they merely adopted the readings of their St source. 138 Although the word is extremely rare in Latin of the classical period (the dictionaries give only Cic. Att. 1,13,1) and I have found no instance in medieval Latin. 139 There is also the possibility that sit had already dropped out in the SI source used by the E revisers (cf. note 137) and that they merely accepted the nominative sentence of this MS. Yet even this explanation seems less likely than that sit dropped out when E was produced. 137

THE E TEXT 81 imply that the nuns' fast should begin on the Friday before Dominica I Quadragesime, whereas the fast regularly began on the Wednesday of the same week (Ash Wednesday); see, for example, KLM 4, pp. 182 ff. It is quite incredible that the Pope would have granted the nuns at Vadstena an exemption of two days in the most important period of fasting without giving any reasons, as the reading quadragesime would imply. The reading quinquagesime implies that the fasting began on the Friday before Shrove Sunday, which only means adding a few days to the regular fasting period.  5.2. THE E TEXT 83 If Sea V legittimaKf Ben; 244-245 communicare K f Ben communicari If Sea V. The distribu- tion among the MSS does not give any real guidance. In § 45g, Ben has et written by a second hand (the dark-ink corrector; see subsection 4.3.3) in an erasure in the line and the word ac has been erased above the line. The ac above the line may have been written by the original scribe (the ink seems to have the brown shade typical of the ink of the original scribe, although it is hard to tell in an erasure), in which case he probably wrote et from the beginning (but his source may have had ac, since he corrected himself). It seems impossible to determine the original reading of Ben with a sufficient degree of reliability. If it was ac, then E also had ac, but if it was et, then E is most likely to have had et, according to the following argumentation. An investigation has revealed that ac was changed to et on three occasions and et to ac on three occasions in the MSS involved (only those passages have been counted in which the conjunctions were indisputably written by the original scribes); of this total of six changes, three appear in the If Sea group, two in V, one only in Kf and none in BO (the tendency is similar as regards other conjunctions). These figures render it more likely that the If Sea group and V got an erroneous ac independently than that Kf and Ben got an erroneous et independently, which in turn is an argument for the reading et; et has been printed. In § 46g the adjective immediato has been adopted, since the adverb does not make sense. In § 92, the Kf Ben reading has been preferred, since the frequency of other transpositions in the If Sea Kf Ben V MSS is in favour of this solution (cf. note 142). In § 217, the If Sea V reading legit- tima et is to be preferred, since BO' dropped et in exactly the same expression in § 215, which indicates that it may be an independent omission in Kf and Ben in § 217. As regards §§ 244-245, the passive form seems to be possible (GMLS and Hammarström), but the Kf Ben reading communicare has been printed, since this form is used elsewhere (viz. in §§ 179, 181, 182 and 247; § 179 is especially important, since the text is recomposed in E and, accordingly, indicates that the E revisers preferred the active form when they had a free choice, just as they had also in §§ 244-245). Furthermore, in §§ 182 and 247, the V MS alone has the error communicari for communicare, which indicates that this error in § 244-245 could very well have been committed independently in an ancestor of If Sea and in V (especially since it may have arisen under the influence of the preceding passive infinitive confiteri). 5.2.5. p Sea BO against Kf V.  86 5. TEXTUAL CRITICISM 5.3. The D text The sto MS has been regarded as the autograph of the 0:14 compilator, since there is nothing against this idea. The text has been restored in the following way. The w MS is reconstructed from Pe Cfa and the v MS from Ne Oe (Oe is re- placed by Ef and so or Rea whenever they have the text). The text of the D MS is then produced from a comparison between (1) v Me but this is a tricky operation since the relations between w v Me could not be specified (subsection 4.5.1). When w v Me agree, they offer the IN text, but when they disagree, one must consider also the readings of the H and E sources which the (1) compi- lator used and the principfes he followed in composing the D text, as weil as syntactical and contextual arguments (cf. note 148). This procedure should be clear from subsections 5.3.1 - 5.3.3 (in smaller type below), in which some more or less doubtful passages are also discussed. The extensive contamination which causes the uncertainty as regards the relations between w v Me implies that the D text cannot be reconstructed with as high a degree of reliability as the other RS texts. 5.3.1. The D compilator had both a H and a E source. This condition is fulfilled in §§ 48-267, in which the D compilator used a lost H MS (= the II source) apparently located in the n group and a lost E MS (= the E source) located in the k group (probably in the x subgroup of 1); the Qe Ue Oa MSS are the best representatives of the compi- lator's lost E source (subsection 4.4.1). In §§ 48-267, the (1) compilator was entirely eclectic, creating almost nothing of his own but merely taking over the text of his sources. In choosing between the two sources, he followed his E source almost slavishly and abandoned it in favour of his II source only in some special passages concerning the status of the RS (subsection 4.4.2). Accordingly, one may define this basic principle: whenever co (represented by Pe Cfa), v (represented by Ne Oe [Ef]) and Me disagree in §§ 48-267, that reading is likely to have been in 0:13 which is backed by Q e Ue Oa (this rule does, of course, not apply to the special passages in which the compilator preferred the II source). A lot of cases have been judged in this way and the Qe ue Oa MSS are then always given in parentheses in the apparatus of the (D text. For examples I refer to subsection 4.5.1: when Pe Cfa have one reading and Ne 06 (Er) Me another, Pe Cfa seem to offer the genuine (1) reading in about half the number of passages and Ne Oe (Er) Me in the other half (examples in subsection 4.5.1 (a)); when Pe Cfa Me agree against Ne Oe (Er), the Pe Cfa Me reading seems generally to have been in D and the Ne Oe (Er) reading very seldom (examples in subsection 4.5.1 (b)); when Pe Cfa Ne Oe (Er) agree against Me, it seems as if b had almost always the Pe Cfa Ne Oe (Er) reading (examples in subsection 4.5.1 (c)); the few passages in which the Me reading is backed by Qe ue Oa are dubious and will be discussed below). The same basic rule has, of course, been applied also when the co v Me groups offer three different readings (for example, 113 N facio Ne Ef [and Qe Ue Oa] talis facio Pe Cfa facio Me; 225 duos calices habeat Pe Cfa [and Qe Ue Oa] duos habeat calices Ne Oe habeat duos calices Me) and when the revisers could have accepted tanto or not. There do not seem to be enough arguments for pleading that the E revisers must have rejected tanto if they encountered this word in their SZ source and for that reason we may accept tanto in the E text. 
 
 
 
 
 5.3. THE .1) TEXT 87 ambiguity as regards (1) is caused not only by discrepancies between the co v Me groups but also to varying extents by doubtfulness as regards the readings in the lost 0.) and/or v MSS (for example, 65 diuinis sororum Cfa Me [and Qe Ue Oa] diuinis Pe Ne Oe; 228 suprascriptis Cfa Ne Oe [and Qe Ue Oa] supradictis Pe Me). Whenever possible, the application of this basic rule should be combined with syntac- tical and contextual evaluations based on the probability that the b compilator would never have taken into his text such readings as are impossible from the point of view of syntax and/or content.148 This is the exact opposite of the procedure in the II text, in which such considerations have a very limited value (section 5.1). For example, in 169 auctoritate Cfa Ef Me (and Qe ue Oa) auctoritatem Pe Ne and 188 absolucione Pe Cfa Ne (and Qe Ue Oa) absolucionem E' Me, the readings auctoritate and absolucione have the advantage from their distribution among the MSS (according to the basic rule) and must have been in (1), since the alternatives are impossible from the point of syntax. In the following part of this subsection, I shall discuss some passages in which the comparisons with Qe ue Oa encounter problems. (a) In 195 monasteriis and 24g nec emittere (complete account in note 107 [for the passages from §§ 6o and 86 in the same note, see (b) below]), the Me readings are backed by Qe Ue Oa and would, accordingly, seem to have an advantage over the Pe Cfa Ne Oe (Er) readings. On the other hand, although no definite stemma diagram can be drawn the Me MS nevertheless seems to be very closely related to the v group (subsection 4.5.1). This means that a reading backed by w v has a greater value than a reading backed by Me alone and it is therefore somewhat hard to adopt the Me readings in 4:0 in g 195 and 249 against the consensus of Pe va Ne Oe (Er l j , especially since the Me text is contaminated from a E MS (subsection 4.5.1) and may have got its readings that way. I have printed, although hesitantly, the Pe Cfa Ne Oe (Ef) readings monasteriis and nec emittere. (b) When the 0113 MSS disagree and one of the presumptive (1) readings is in Qe ue and another in 0a, that reading has generally been adopted which is backed by Q e Ue, since Qe Ue are closer to the E source than Ou (subsection 4.4.i), for example, 5o attrectare Pe Cfa Ne Oe (and Qe Ue) attractare Me (and 0e); 85 aperire potest fenestram Pe Cfa Me (and Qe Ue) aperiri potest fenestra Ne Oe (and 0a);1" 90 eciam Va Ne Oe (and Qe Ue) autem Me (and Oa) deest Pe; other passages of this kind (cf. the apparatus): 93 piscibus,"° 138 expauescas, 151 ad, 164 preterquam, 191 deferant, 234 quo (ante cor- poris)150, 244-245 confiteri communicare, 247 possint (ante minime). On two occasions, however, Qe Ue back Me and Oe backs Pe Cfa Ne Oe: 6o vtilitatis Pe Cfa Ne Oe (and Ou) vtilitatis et Me (and Qe Ue); 86 ieiuniis monialium Pe Cfa Ne Oe (and 0a) ieiuniis Me 148 It seems reasonable to assume that the b compilator never accepted readings which were impossible when judged from the viewpoint of syntax and/or content. Yet, since he was merely eclectic and almost never changed the readings of his sources (subsection 4.4.2), he might have accepted readings which were not perfect as regarded content and syntax from the sources. One should, accordingly, try to avoid rejecting any reading merely because it seems to be somewhat inferior to an alternative reading; the inferior reading might have been in D, the better reading being a conjecture at a lower point in the stemma. 149 Anyway, this passage seems to imply some contamination, since neither the consensus between Pe Cfa Me and Qe Ue nor the consensus between Ne Oe and Oct are likely to be ac- cidental. 150 In § 93, the Pe Ca Oa reading in piscibus is syntactically impossible, which is another quite reliable indication that this reading was not in 0. In a similar way, when one of the presumptive D readings is in Qe Oa and another in Ue, the reading backed by Qe Ou has been printed, for example, 135 conuertet Cfa Ne Er (and Qe Ou) conuertat Pe Me (and Ue); other similar passages: 136 stabiliat, 213 in monasterio. 5.3.2. The D compilator had only a n source. This condition is fulfilled in §§ 1 - 34, 42-44 and 271-317 and the H source was located in the n group (subsection 4.4.1). In these paragraphs, the D text deviates more often from the n MSS than from the Qe Ue Oa MSS in §§ 48-267; the reason may be either that the I compilator fels more free to re-arrange the text in these paragraphs or, as is perhaps more likely, that his lost H source was different from the extant i1 MSS and already had the b readings in such passages (subsection 4.4.3). The following basic rule has been applied: whenever the D MSS (pe Cfa Ne Oe [SO Rea] Me) give unreliable information on the reading of (1), that reading among those offered by the 1 MSS has been printed which is backed by the n group of ri (represented by p7 [whenever pY has the text] K P in the apparatus of the H text). Examples: 34 statim ad me Pe Cfa Me (and pY K P) ad me statim Ne Sen; 297 quod (ante denegetur) Ne Sen (and pY K P) vt Pe Cfa cui Me. Syntax and content should always be taken into consideration, as described in note 148, for example, 287 paulatim se redire Pe C fa Me (and pY K [paulatim ante senserunt loc. Kl P) paulatim Ne Sen (complete account in subsection 4.5. i); se redire has the support of the MSS and was certainly in 40, since the syntax and content are in disorder without these words. In the following part of this subsection, I shall 1 discuss some passages in which the comparisons with the n MSS encounter problems. (a) When Pe Cfa agree against Ne Sen (Ren) Me, that reading has generally been adopted which is backed by the n group, in full accordance with the basic rule outlined above, for example, 291 ego sum filius dei viui Ne Sen Me (and IV K P) om. Pe Cfa; 32 vel ardore Pe Ge (and pY K P) et ardore Ne Sen Me. The objection could be raised that the w text is probably contaminated from a II source and that such a contamination seems to have affected also the v Me texts together (subsection 4.5.i). This contamination could ex- plain the coincidence between Ne Sen Me pY K P and between Pe Ck' p7 K P respectively in the passages under discussion, thus rendering this coincidence useless in determining the D reading. The problem is similar to the one concerning Me in subsection 5.3.1 (a); in the passages dealt with there I rejected (with hesitation) the Me readings backed by Qe Ue 0%151 but here I have (with hesitation) adopted the readings backed by the n In a similar way the Me reading has been rejected in 316 asinus staret Pe Ne Sen staret asinus Me (and pY K P) deest G. 151 
 
 
 
 
 5.3. THE (1) TEXT 89 MSS. The reason for this difference is that, in the constellation Pe Cfa Ne Oe (Ef) against Me, the Pe Cfa Ne Oe (Er) readings already have an advantage from the distribution itself (subsection 5.3.1 (a)) whereas there is no such advantage for any of the readings in the distribution Pe Cfa against Ne sen (Ren) Me dealt with here. On two occasions, however, in §§ 306-317 a reading backed by the t MSS has been rejected. Paragraphs 306-317 are missing in Cfa, the Pe MS being the only representative of w, and it happens twice that a Pe reading is backed by the n MSS: 310 poterit Ne sen Me potest Pe (and pY K P); 317 eam confestim Ne Me confestim Sef confestim eam Pe (and pY K P). Since it seemed hard to adopt a reading backed by Pe only within the F group, the readings poterit and eam confestim have been printed, although the passages are dubious. (b) The decision is difficult whenever the D MSS offer two readings, both of which may have been in cp and both of which are also in the ii MSS. Since there is no guidance from the ii MSS in such passages, I have taken the Ne sen (Ren) Me readings whenever these MSS agree against Pe Cfa (9 ac multi alii [complete account in subsection 4.2.5], 15 multas vineas [yet Sen omitted multas], 287 laus ... amen, 302 mi domine; cf. the apparatus of the ID and H texts for these passages). In 282 sicut si, this reading has been taken with the support of Pe Me (and pY P) against Ne Sen (and K) (Cia has sicut si with si above the line). In 296 incomparabilis Ne sen (and pY) incorporalis Me (in ras. K2 P) incorporabilis Pe Cfa, the choice is between incomparabilis and incorporalis and the former alternative has been chosen (cf. subsection 5.1.2). (c) The reconstruction of the incipit in § i is difficult and the incipits of the Pe Cfa Ne Oe Me MSS are given in extenso in the apparatus. 5.3.3. The D compilator had neither a n nor a E source. This condition is fulfilled in §§ 35-41 and the text must be established from the D MSS alone. Passages in which Pe Cfa agree against Ne Sen (Ren) me are problematic, viz. the heading in § 35 (see the apparatus) and 38 ne Ne sen Me vt ne Pe Cfa; 39 creator Ne Sen Me conditor pe Cfa; 41 tibi nunc Ne Sen me tibi pe Cfa; the Ne Sen (Ren) Me readings have been printed in these passages. In 37 habebitur Ne sen habeatur Pe Cfa habetur (in habebitur corr.) Me, the Ne Sen reading has been preferred out of the three alternatives. The paragraphs under discussion appear also as Ex. 46 (edited by Hollman on p. 162); the text from the Extrauagantes backs the Pe Cfa readings in §§ 39, 41 and 37 and the Ne Sen Me reading in § 38, but this is not decisive, since the relation between RS D 35-42 and Ex. 46 could not be specified.152 5.3.4. In F, however, these seven revelations were numbered 1-7, as is clear from Fig. 21 above, and the numbers carried additions indicating that the chapters formed a collection of revelations concerning the RS called Reuelaciones super regulam; such additions are marked sr in Fig. 21 and the distribution reveals that they were already in 0.156 The collection Reuelaciones super regulam does not end with § 317 but continues with several other revelations which have not been printed here, since they are already available in other editions (note 28). I have assumed that the Reuelaciones super regulam collection was composed by the D compilator but it cannot be excluded that this collection already existed as an independent collection when he brought the 0 version of the RS together. Finally, the Reuelaciones super regulam collection, with §§ 42-267 embedded in it, is preceded by §§ 5—I 1, which form a proheme (cf. the end of § i) without any chapter number; the Ref3 numbering reuelacio prima super regulam is erroneous, since Rei3 (to- gether with Ne Oe Me) has this numbering also for the following chapter (§§ 13-21). 5.4. The 0 text The lost 0 MS is the bull sealed and issued by the papal chancellery and after- wards kept at Vadstena. The reconstruction is concentrated only on this docu- ment, which had legal validity, not on some draft in the chancellery which must have been behind it. There exist five independent branches from 0 (the connection of DO is dubious and it is open to doubt whether it constitutes a branch of its own or not) and in the edition they have been represented by Qf, Bea, Sf, pa and Tf respectively (Tf is replaced by Def3 when it lacks the text and when the text is more or less worn out). Normalizations The name of St. Birgitta has throughout been normalized to Birgitta and varia- tions of spelling have not been listed in the apparatus. Other names also appear in one and the same form throughout the four texts edited, viz. the form which has the best support in the MSS used for their establishment, and varia- tions of spelling in these MSS are completely accounted for in the apparatus (even minor details). The Trinitarian formula In nomine Patris et Filii et Spiritus Sancti. Amen. has been normalized, but variations in the MSS have been re- corded in the apparatus.162 The numbers of the chapters have been normalized in the form Capitulum / etc. and consistently placed after the headings. In the apparatus are listed only variations of the figure as such, not deviations in wording and location, nor is it specified whether the figure is written in Roman or Arabic numerals or in words. Additions to the chapter numbers indicating that the chapter belonged to the Reuelaciones super regulam collection have been normalized in the form of Reuelacio oo super regulam (see note 156). Figures in the current text are always printed in words (for example, RS II E ID 1 73 tredecim); variations of the figure as such are accounted for but not whether the figure is in Roman or Arabic numerals or in words. For normalizations as regards the orthography, see section 5.7. 5.7. Orthography The MSS used to establish the RS texts present very much the same ortho- graphic variations as the MSS used in the previous editions of the Birgitta In connection with H and E, it should be mentioned that OSAa lacks the headings of the prayers. Since they were certainly in II and E (anyway in most of the passages), they must have been dropped when the OSA" text was produced (or maybe it was translated from a Latin MS which [like In] lacked the headings). 162 The formula appears in RS II E (1) 109, 116, 119, 121, 123, 125, 127, 130, 132, 134, 136, 138 and 266. In Be0, the expression is generally abbreviated (normally in noe p. et f. et ss.) and a second hand (cf. subsection 4.3.3) added explanations above the line in most of the passages; these additions in Be 0 are not accounted for in the apparatus. 161 
 
 
 
 
 5.7. ORTHOGRAPHY 95 corpus and I refer to them for examples (Undhagen, pp. 168 ff.; Hollman, pp. 107 if.; Bergh, Rev. VII, pp. 98 f., and Rev. V, p. 72; Eklund, SA, pp. 55 ff.). In the present edition the standards of the previous editions have mainly been adopted. The ancient classical spelling (Georges) forms the basis, but deviations from it have been accepted when they are frequent in the MSS. Some of these deviations have been entered in all words in which they appear throughout the texts (just as in the previous editions): e is used for ae and oe, ci is used for ti before vowels (not when ti is preceded by t or s), v is used initially and u otherwise for both the consonant and the vowel. Other deviations have been accepted in words in which they have very strong support from the MSS163 (for example, consumare, legittime, michi, nichil, dampnacio, elemosina, dyabolus, misterium). The same principle has been adopted as regards word division, for example, II 05 298 quo ad, 0 327 ab extra as two words with the MSS. Ortho- graphic details have generally not been listed in the apparatus. 163 When a deviation from the classical spelling of a word gives the impression of being frequent in the MSS, the frequency has been examined in this way. All occurrences of the word in the 1-1 E01:0 and 0 texts have been checked in all the MSS on which the texts are based. When the deviation is present in more than 6o % of all the instances thus gathered, it has been adopted in the printed text. 
 
 
 
 
 6. The apparatus The critical apparatus is built up in the usual way and conclusions may be drawn e silentio concerning the MSS listed as "codices adhibiti" at the beginning of each chapter of the text. In the apparatus of the II text are given the readings of the Old Swedish MS OSA• in parentheses when it facilitates the reconstruc- tion of the H text (subsection 5.1.i) and in a similar way the apparatus of the (I) text often contains the readings of the E MSS Qe Ue O• in parentheses since these MSS are good representatives of the (1) compilator's E source (subsection 5.3.0; no conclusions whatsoever may be drawn e silentio concerning the OSA• Qe Ue 0a MSS, since they are adduced only when the H and D MSS do not give sufficient information. When a correction was apparently not made by the original scribe himself but afterwards by someone else, this has been marked by index figures (for example, RS H 4 capitulum / om. Ceal suppl. Cea2; for the different correctors in Be0, see subsection 4.3.3); when this issue cannot be settled (as is often the case in microfilms and photocopies), such information is not given (for example, RS H 51 ex incestura in intestura corr. P). For the account of variations in names and other expressions which have been normalized in the texts, see section 5.6. Orthographic details are generally not listed in the apparatus (cf. section 5.7). In another apparatus have been collected references to the introduction concerning those of the passages dealt with in the introduction in which the establishment of the text requires some discussion.

 I I2 7. THE II TEXT dicatur ei: roo 'Filia, quandoque sub specie boni latet falsitatis laqueus et inconsideracio futurorum multos supplantat. Reuertere ergo ad nos i0 post aliquos menses et ostende nobis desiderium tuum, si perseuerat in bono!' ror Reuertente ergo illa et humiliante se sicut prius, predicentur ei dura et aspera ordinis, contemptus mundi et obliuio parentum. Que omnia si se seruaturam promiserit, tunc circa finem anni omnis congre- gacio consenciet in eam. 102 Que si talis persona fuerit, quod de eius 15 vita non est dubium, in ipso principio peticionis eius omnes consentire possunt in eam sed ante annum ad introitum et professionen seu habi- tus recepcionem nullatenus admittatur. 103 Adepto itaque consensu ingressionis mittatur pro episcopo, qui rogatus veniens consecrabit eam. 104 Veniens autem episcopus descendet ad ianuam ecclesie; et eam, que 20 religionem ingressura est, expectantem episcopus ante fores interroget dicens: 'Es tu libera et ab omni vinculo ecclesie immunis, scilicet coniu- gii, voti et excommunicacionis?' ros Que si responderit: 'Vere libera sum', subiungat episcopus: 'Numquid pudor aut forte dolor mundane aduersitatis compellit te ad religionem? Aut forte copia debitorum tuo- 25 rum non solutorum coartat te?' THE H TEXT Christus determinat hic numerum monialium et sacerdotum et dya- conorum ac eciam conuersorum seruiencium dicto conuentui et ordinat habitacionem eorum et chorum, vbi sedere et stare debeant tam mares quam femine. 149 Capitulum XII. 148 5 150 » Sorores erunt sexaginta et non plures. Que clericos habebunt, qui cottidie de tempore missam et officium, quod habetur in ecclesiis cathedralibus illarum terrarum, in quibus huiusmodi monasteria sunt, decantabunt. 151 Ipsi quidem a monasterio sororum sint omnino exclusi vnam per se habentes curiam, in qua habitabunt, et de curia io introitum in ecclesiam et chorum inferiorem habebunt. Chorus vero sororum erit superius sub tecto, ita tamen quod sacramenta videre et officium audire valeant. 152 Ipsi quidem sacerdotes debent esse tre- decim iuxta numerum tredecim apostolorum, quorum Paulus, tercius decimus, non minimum laborem sustinuit; deinde quatuor dyaconi, qui 15 eciam sacerdotes possunt esse, si volunt, et ipsi figuram habent quatuor precipuorum doctorum, Ambrosii, Augustini, Gregorii et Ieronimi; 153 deinde octo laici, qui laboribus suis clericis necessaria ministrabunt. THE 11 TEXT 244 Christus disponit hic de modo fenestrarum seu cratis et declarat, quod moniales possint ibidem audiri sed non videri tempore confessionis, tempore vero communionis possint audiri pariter et videri. 245 Dicit eciam de rota et de modo ibidem tenendo et prohibet, quod nullus vmquam confessor vel alius intret monasterium monialium, nisi quando alicui infirme danda sunt sacramenta aut quando aliqua mortua debeat extrahi ad sepeliendum. 246 Capitulum XXV . 247 »Sorores confessiones suas faciant ad fenestras ita ordinatas, quod audiri quidem possint, minime autem videri. Communicare vero debent io ad fenestras, vbi audiri possint pariter et videri. 248 Sed quando de aliis corporis aut anime commodis confessori aut alicui presbiterorum seu fratrum loqui voluerint, tunc ad alias fenestras, vbi audiri eciam possunt sed non videri, sedeant. 249 Ibi in pariete rota quedam habeatur, per quam accipienda et mittenda sunt necessaria. Nulla tamen sororum ibi 15 aliqua loqui vel audire presumat nec accipere aliqua vel emittere sine scitu vel licencia abbatisse. 250 Caueatur eciam ibi et in omni loco, nisi dum confessiones ad fenestras deputatas audiuntur, ne aliqua soror ad audiendum siue loquendum alicui sine presencia aliquarum sororum inueniatur sola, que omnia verba audient sicut ipsa. 251 Prohibeatur 20 eciam, ne vmquam confessor seu aliquis presbiterorum aut fratrum monasterium ingrediatur, nisi quando infirmis donanda sunt sacramenta. Tunc autem ingrediatur confessor sed nullo modo solus ymmo aliquibus ipsum sequentibus. 252 Mortua vero aliqua sorore omnes presbiteri et fratres cum confessore ingrediantur cum cantu et oracionibus corpus ad sepulchrum deferendo.» 25 Codices adhibiti: §§ 244-252: p13 Pf K P Cea Gh i disposuit pa — 2 ex audire in audiri corr.  H 244-261 5 131 253 Christus ordinat hic, quod dyocesanus episcopus sit pater et visitator monasterii istius religionis, princeps vero regni seu prouincie debeat esse defensor et papa earum tutor caritatiuus, sine cuius licencia nullum monasterium istius religionis fundetur. 254 Dicit eciam, quod aliqui deuoti fratres de regula beati Benedicti aut beati Bernardi addant in ista regula aliqua capitula super correccione excessuum et super visitacione fienda et super omnibus aliis, que huic regule necessaria viderint expedire. 255 Capitulum XX VI. 256 »Episcopus, in cuius dyocesi monasterium est, erit tam sororum io quam fratrum pater et visitator necnon et iudex in omnibus causis seu casibus sorores aut fratres tangentibus. 257 Ipsum denique oportet continue sollicitum et diligentem esse speculatorem, si regula in omni- bus punctis obseruatur, ne contingat ipsius salubria statuta ab aliquibus sororum aut fratrum paruipendi. 258 Princeps regni seu terre, in qua est 15 monasterium, erit eis responsalis et defensor in omnibus necessitatibus. Papa vero super vtrumque, scilicet principem terre et episcopum, erit eorum tutor caritatiuus, si eius adiutorium postulauerint necessitate aliqua compellente. 259 Quicumque monasterium huius religionis construere voluerit, nullatenus sine voluntate et licencia pape hoc 20 presumat. 26o Deinde ista regula per papam confirmata inquirantur aliqui deuoti fratres de regulis Benedicti vel Bernardi, qui huic regule inscribant, quomodo excessus emendandi sunt in monasterio et quo- modo mortui sepeliendi sunt et qualiter visitabit episcopus et pro quibus casibus ingredietur monasterium. 261 Et omnia alia necessaria, que in 25 hiis verbis non narrantur, ad huius regule roboracionem assumantur de regulis supradictis. » Codices adhibiti: §§ 253-261: po P' K P Cea Gh 1 rubrica ista debet esse de rubro ante christus add. THE II TEXT 304 Christus loquens sponse dicit ei, quod ipsa laboret taliter, quod dicta regula per dominum papam confirmetur, promittens graciam et adiutorium omnibus intrantibus istam religionem et augmentum pacis et concordie in patria illa, vbi aliquod monasterium istius religionis fundatum fuerit. 305 Capitulum XXX/. 5 306 Deinde vox, que prius loquebatur, respondit dicens: »Ego sine principio sum et sine fine et omnia secundum voluntatem meam ordi- naui et, sicut michi placuit, omnia feci. 307 Vnde, si quis interrogaret, quare non prius creaui celum et terram et omnia, que in eis sunt, io respondendum esset, quia sic fuit voluntas mea. 308 Similiter, si quere- retur, quare non prius istam regulam dedi aut confirmari eam volui, respondendum est, quia sic volui. Nonne dicit scriptura: 'Spiritus, vbi vult, spirat.' Sic vere est. Ipse enim spirat diuersis modis, vbi vult et quando vult. 309 Ipsum tales sequentur consolaciones, vt totum cor 15 repentina repletur leticia, que de nullis mundanis seu corporalibus rebus cordi aduenit sed ex Spiritus gracia tunc inspirantis. 310 Ergo, si papa talia in corde suo senserit, quando hanc regulam coram se legi audierit, tunc intelligere potest, vnde regula venerit. Ideo nulli licitum sit habere aliquod proprium, nullam omnino rem quamuis minimam, sed nec obulum io quidem possidere vel attractare manibus 51 nec auri quid habere vel argenti, nisi forte pro intextura alicuius operis auri vel argenti tactu opus sit et hoc eciam non absque consilio et licencia abbatisse. 52 Omnia autem necessaria de abbatissa speranda sunt, scilicet indumenta regu- laria, lectisternia et instrumenta operis, nec quicquam habeant, quod is regula non permittit. 53 De lectisterniis. 54 Capitulum 11. 5 55 Sciendum est autem, quod lectisternia regularia esse debent de straminibus.  §§ 47-64 1 47 56 De indumentis sororum. 57 Capitulum III. 58 Indumenta vero sororum sunt due camisie de albo burello, vna propter cottidianum vsum, alia propter locionem, vna tunica de burello griseo et vna cuculla, cuius manice non longius quam ad summitatem 5 medii digiti protendantur. 59 Et dependentes sinus circa manum, quando manualia seruicia exercebunt, cum nodo instar aliarum manica- rum moderate ad brachia constringantur. Vnum eciam mantellum habendum est de burello griseo sicut tunica et cuculla. 6o Quod quidem mantellum non deforis corrugatum nec accurate compositum sed ex io parte strictum et planum, totum habens vtilitatis et nichil vanitatis. Quod eciam in estate debet esse simplex, in hyeme vero sufforatum non pellibus delicatis sed agninis vel ouinis. 61 De pellibus eciam huiusmodi pellicium in hyeme haberi potest. Ipsum quoque mantellum ab vno palmo terram non pertingat et nodo ligneo in pectore collagetur. Ad 1 5 calciamenta autem pedum in estate habeant sotulares vsque ad talos et pedulos vsque ad genua 62 in hyeme vero sotulares vsque ad genua altos, sufforatos burello, et pedulos eque altos. Ornamenta capitis erit vitta, qua frons et gene circumdentur et ex parte operiatur facies; cuius extremitates vna acus in occipite coniungat. 63 Super hanc ponatur 20 velum de tela denigrata, quod ne defluat, tres acus adaptabunt, vna circa frontem et due circa ambas aures. Deinde super velum ponatur corona de tela alba, cui assuantur quinque particule de panno rubeo quasi quinque gutte; 64 prima particula sit in fronte, altera in occipite, tercia et quarta circa aures, quinta in medio capitis in modum crucis. Hanc 25 coronam vna acus in medio capitis stabiliet et capiti coaptabit.  §§ 141-157 148 De numero sororum et fratrum et conuersorum. 159 149 Capitulum X. Sorores erunt sexaginta et non plures. Que clericos habebunt, qui cottidie de tempore missam et officium, quod habetur in ecclesiis cathedralibus illarum terrarum, in quibus huiusmodi monasteria sunt, 5 decantabunt. 151 Ipsi quidem a monasterio sororum sint omnino separati vnam per se habentes curiam, in qua habitabunt, et de curia introitum in ecclesiam et chorum inferiorem habebunt. Chorus vero sororum erit superius sub tecto, ita tamen quod sacramenta videre et officium audire valeant. 152 Ipsi quidem sacerdotes debent esse tredecim iuxta numerum io tredecim apostolorum, quorum Paulus, tercius decimus, non minimum laborem sustinuit; deinde quatuor dyaconi, qui eciam sacerdotes possunt esse, si volunt, et ipsi figuram habent quatuor precipuorum doctorum, Ambrosii, Augustini, Gregorii et Ieronimi; /53 deinde octo laici, qui laboribus suis clericis necessaria ministrabunt. Computatis 15 igitur sexaginta sororibus, tredecim sacerdotibus, quatuor dyaconis et octo eorum seruitoribus tantus omnium personarum erit numerus, quantus erat tredecim apostolorum et septuaginta duorum discipulorum. 150 154 De habitu fratrum et sacerdotum. 155 Capitulum XI.  161 §§ 158-174 x65 De eleccione abbatisse et confessoris generalis monasterii. 166 Capitulum XII. Abbatissa eligatur a conuentu; electa vero legittime ab episcopo confirmetur. Omnia tamen opera sua faciant cum consilio et licencia abbatisse. 237 Numquid ipse Christus, dominus omnium, fuit in mundo sine labore? Numquid non laborauit eundo, docendo, paciendo? Numquid apostoli fuerunt sine labore, quibus 15 per omnia potuisset Deus sufficienter dedisse? Qua finita vnus dericorum vocet eam ad altare dicens: 'Procede, sponsa Christi, ad altare Christit 14o Ipsa igitur procedens humiliet se ad veniam super faciem suam et episcopus flexis genibus cum clericis suis legat go letaniam orando omnes sanctos pro famula Dei. 141 Finitis autem letaniis episcopus surgens ad famulam Dei accedat prostratam et legat super eam absolucionem peccatorum.  195 §§ 140-153 148 De numero sacerdotum, sororum, dyaconorum et laicorum. 149 Capi- tulum X. 150 »Sorores erunt sexaginta et non plures. Que clericos habebunt, qui cottidie de tempore missam et officium, quod habetur in ecclesiis 5 cathedralibus illarum terrarum, in quibus huiusmodi monasteria sunt, decantabunt. 151 Ipsi quidem a monasterio sororum omnino sint separati vnam habentes per se curiam, in qua habitabunt, et de curia introitum ad ecclesiam et chorum inferiorem habebunt. Chorus vero sororum erit superius sub tecto, ita tamen quod sacramenta videre et officium audire I° valeant. 152 Ipsi quidem sacerdotes debent esse tredecim iuxta nume- rum tredecim apostolorum, quorum Paulus, tercius decimus, non mini- mum laborem sustinuit; deinde quatuor dyaconi, qui eciam sacerdotes possunt esse, si volunt, et ipsi figuram habent quatuor precipuorum doctorum, Ambrosii, Augustini, Gregorii et Ieronimi; 153 deinde octo 15 laici, qui laboribus suis clericis necessaria ministrabunt. THE (I) TEXT modum. 235 Sic sorores omni tempore, quo diuinis non intersunt vel leccioni vel tale tempus fuerit, quod licite laborare possint, tunc eciam manibus suis laborent, vt, sicut michi seruiunt ore, sic seruiant et reliquis membris. 236 Et iste labor non sit ad aliquam mundi vanitatem, I° non ad aliquod lucrum proprium sed, sicut labor Matris mee, pro honore meo et ecclesiarum et pauperum vtilitate. Omnia tamen opera sua faciant cum consilio et licencia abbatisse. 237 Numquid ego ipse, Domi- nus omnium, fui in mundo sine labore? Numquid non laboraui eundo, docendo, paciendo? Numquid apostoli mei fuerunt sine labore, quibus 15 bene per omnia potuissem sufficienter dedisse?  PART C Indices 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 231 11. Index of words In the following list have been indexed those words which are not in K. E. Georges's Ausfiihrliches Lateinisch-Deutsches Handwörterbuch 1-2 (Han- over & Leipzig 1913-1918) and also some words which are, indeed, in Georges's lexicon but have meanings which differ considerably from those listed there. No words are included here which differ from those in Georges's lexicon only as regards their spellings. Whenever a meaning of an indexed word is so frequent in mediaeval texts that it has been recorded in the majority of the current dictionaries of mediaeval Latin, no reference to any suck dictionary is given in the list; when a meaning is less frequent, references are given in parentheses and the abbreviations in smaller type below have been used for this purpose; it is always mentioned explicitly when a word or its meaning is in none of the current dictionaries. Matth. 21,2; Marc. 11,2; Luc. 19,30. aliaque necessaria ab 334 calciamenta aliis quam ab abbatissa propria ... petere non presumant, cf. Bened. reg. 33,5.
